             <h1>
              80beats
             </h1>
             <p class="credit">
             </p>
            </div>

          <div class="singlepost">
           <div class="post" id="post-main-39394">
            <div class="entry">
             <div class="navigation">
              <span class="prev">
               
               <a href="http://blogs.discovermagazine.com/80beats/2012/08/22/mayan-tree-chopping-may-have-worsened-droughts-and-contributed-to-the-civilizations-demise/" rel="prev">
                Mayan Tree Chopping May Have Worsened Droughts, and Contributed to The Civilization's Demise
               </a>
              </span>
              <span class="next">
               <a href="http://blogs.discovermagazine.com/80beats/2012/08/23/older-dads-pass-on-more-mutations-to-their-kids/" rel="next">
                Older Dads Pass on More Mutations to Their Kids
               </a>
               
              </span>
             </div>
             <h1 class="post-title single">
              <a href="http://blogs.discovermagazine.com/80beats/2012/08/23/look-at-this-glowing-south-american-roaches-mimic-toxic-beetles/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Look at This: Glowing South American Roaches Mimic Toxic Beetles">
               Look at This: Glowing South American Roaches Mimic Toxic Beetles
              </a>
             </h1>
             <div class="meta">
              <span class="meta-date">
               By
               <a href="http://discovermagazine.com/authors?name=Veronique+Greenwood" style="color:#555">
                Veronique Greenwood
               </a>
               | 
		August 23, 2012 10:25 am
              </span>
             </div>
             <div class="shareIcons" style="border-top:1px solid #999;border-bottom:1px solid #999;padding:7px 0 7px 0;margin-bottom:20px;">
              <div class="addthis_toolbox addthis_default_style addthis_32x32_style">
               <a class="addthis_button_preferred_1">
               </a>
               <a class="addthis_button_preferred_2">
               </a>
               <a class="addthis_button_preferred_3">
               </a>
               <a class="addthis_button_preferred_4">
               </a>
               <a class="addthis_button_compact">
               </a>
               <a class="addthis_counter addthis_bubble_style">
               </a>
              </div>
             </div>
             <p class="imgcapright">
              <img alt="roaches" src="http://blogs.discovermagazine.com/80beats/files/2012/08/glowing-roaches.jpg"/>
             </p>
             <p>
              Under normal light, this roach looks normal enough. But under a fluorescent light, its three spotstwo large ones and one very tiny one just visible under the right spotlight up like a Christmas tree.
             </p>
             <p>
              This remarkable species of South American cockroach,
              <em>
               Lucihormetica luckae,
              </em>
              owes its fluorescence to bacteria. The spots on the dark brown area of its carapace are pits inhabited by microbes that glow under fluorescent light.
             </p>
             <p>
              <span id="more-39394">
              </span>
              A
              <a href="http://www.springerlink.com/content/61g4j8206wln0532/">
               recent analysis
              </a>
              of these creatures bioluminescence demonstrates that they and their cousin species glow at the same wavelengths as a toxin-producing beetle that lives in their area, suggesting that the roaches are mimicking a deadly neighbor to avoid getting picked off by predators. However, it may not be predators these roaches need to worry most about: its habitat destruction. No specimens have been found since the volcano they live on erupted two years ago.
             </p>
             <p>
              <em>
               Image courtesy of Vransk et al., Naturwissenschaften (2012)
              </em>
             </p>
             <div style="clear:both;">
             </div>

                <!-- #comment-## -->
                <li class="comment odd alt thread-odd thread-alt depth-1" id="dsq-comment-34035">
                 <div class="dsq-comment-header" id="dsq-comment-header-34035">

                <!-- #comment-## -->
                <li class="comment even thread-even depth-1" id="dsq-comment-34036">
                 <div class="dsq-comment-header" id="dsq-comment-header-34036">
                  <cite id="dsq-cite-34036">
                   <span id="dsq-author-user-34036">
                    Ian Jamie
                   </span>
                  </cite>
                 </div>
                 <div class="dsq-comment-body" id="dsq-comment-body-34036">
                  <div class="dsq-comment-message" id="dsq-comment-message-34036">
                   <p>
                    semi: Luminescence is a catch-all term for any sort of light emission not generated by heat (e.g., incandescent bulbs, red-hot objects). Fluorescence is a subset of this. It refers to emission of light after excitation (irradiation) by light  most commonly experienced as (but not confined to) emission of visible light after excitation by ultraviolet light. Bioluminescence is luminescence from biological systems, hence a fluorescent, living creature is exhibiting bioluminescence.
                   </p>
                  </div>
                 </div>
                </li>
                <!-- #comment-## -->
                <li class="comment odd alt thread-odd thread-alt depth-1" id="dsq-comment-34037">
                 <div class="dsq-comment-header" id="dsq-comment-header-34037">
                  <cite id="dsq-cite-34037">
                   <span id="dsq-author-user-34037">
                    hilarleo
                   </span>
                  </cite>
                 </div>
                 <div class="dsq-comment-body" id="dsq-comment-body-34037">
                  <div class="dsq-comment-message" id="dsq-comment-message-34037">
                   <p>
                    Well-spotted! What semi said!
                    <br/>
                    Bioluminescence and fluorescence are discrete abilities, yet this micro-article appears to use the terms indiscriminately. At least the article is confusing.     But  I can  dig it- Bio-anything is trendy.
                   </p>
                   <p>
                    So then- Whats the roach doing? This article is unclear. For the sake of definitions:
                    <br/>
                    Bioluminescence, in conventional usage, means any biological process which generates some light, as found in certain bacteria, insects, pelagic fishes and several zooplankton. Bioluminescence is not dependent on or related to fluorescence and can employ all the colors of the rainbow, but often dominated by characteristic greens.
                    <br/>
                    Fluorescence is the enhanced, spectrum-shifted reflectivity of certain minerals and pigments.  Typically mineral fluorescence appears white; But  a limited range of fluorescent mineral colors are known.
                   </p>
                   <p>
                    The article muddies it all, suggesting  this biology depends on fluorescent light (which itself uses novel fluorescent processes and a variety of gas-tube environments- but not reliably producing specific wavelengths) as if every glowing thing involved mysterious fluorescent minerals.
                   </p>
                   <p>
                    But our Science is alive! Humans continue to discover more more forms of luminance regularly. Knowing this- Its the fun stuff! Not difficult. Lets all keep it meaningful.
                    <br/>
                    And so where now is our perfect automated Editor?
                   </p>
                  </div>
                 </div>
                </li>

var disqus_title = "Look at This: Glowing South American Roaches Mimic Toxic Beetles";
var disqus_config_custom = window.disqus_config;
var disqus_config = function () {
    /*
    All currently supported events:
    onReady: fires when everything is ready,
    onNewComment: fires when a new comment is posted,
    onIdentify: fires when user is authenticated
    */
    
    
    this.language = '';
        this.callbacks.onReady.push(function () {

        // sync comments in the background so we don't block the page
        var script = document.createElement('script');
        script.async = true;
        script.src = '?cf_action=sync_comments&amp;post_id=39394';

        var firstScript = document.getElementsByTagName('script')[0];
        firstScript.parentNode.insertBefore(script, firstScript);
    });
    
    if (disqus_config_custom) {
        disqus_config_custom.call(this);
    }
};

(function() {
    var dsq = document.createElement('script'); dsq.type = 'text/javascript';
    dsq.async = true;
    dsq.src = '//' + disqus_shortname + '.disqus.com/embed.js';
    (document.getElementsByTagName('head')[0] || document.getElementsByTagName('body')[0]).appendChild(dsq);
})();
             </script>

          <script type="text/javascript">
           /* &lt;![CDATA[ */
		(function() {
			var dropdown = document.getElementById('discoverblog_categories');
			function onCatChange() {
				if ( dropdown.options[dropdown.selectedIndex].value &gt; 0 ) {
					location.href = "http://blogs.discovermagazine.com/80beats/?cat="+dropdown.options[dropdown.selectedIndex].value;
				}
			}
			dropdown.onchange = onCatChange;
		})();

		(function() {
			var dropdown = document.getElementById('discoverblog_tags');
			function onCatChange() {
				if (dropdown.options[dropdown.selectedIndex].value) {
					location.href = dropdown.options[dropdown.selectedIndex].value;
				}
			}
			dropdown.onchange = onCatChange;
		})();

		(function() {
			var dropdown = document.getElementById('discoverblog_archives');
			function onCatChange() {
				if (dropdown.options[dropdown.selectedIndex].value) {
					location.href = dropdown.options[dropdown.selectedIndex].value;
				}
			}
			dropdown.onchange = onCatChange;
		})();
	/* ]]&gt; */
          </script>
